  **PART 1a — DONE (this commit): the classification logic, shipped as live + verified code.** New `mackesd_core::worker_role` module — `WORKER_TIERS` census (all 31), `min_rank`/`runs`/`workers_for_rank`, `resolve_rank` (pinned rank, else Workstation when unpinned, else Lighthouse when malformed). 7 unit tests pin the 11/3/17 split + the superset property + the fail-closed policy. Made live + runtime-verifiable by a `mackesd role-workers [<role>]` diagnostic (the static counterpart to the live worker-status): `mackesd role-workers {lighthouse,server,workstation}` prints 11/14/31 workers (verified), unknown role errors. `mde-role` added as a non-optional mackesd dep.
  **PART 1b — NEXT (the run_serve spawn-gating itself).** Bigger than first estimated — **52** `sup.spawn` calls across a ~1250-line region (3189–4433), with nested conditionals + sub-spawns + the interspersed Bus-responder/Nebula blocks, of which 31 are the named `worker_names` workers. Gate each named spawn+push pair with `if mackesd_core::worker_role::runs("n", role_rank)` after one `let role_rank = worker_role::resolve_rank();` at the top of the worker section. The logic + classification are already done (part 1a) + unit-tested, so 1b is mechanical gating + a live `worker-status`-per-role bench check. **Reviewed tier table** (interpretation: §12's role *definitions* govern — a Lighthouse IS a VPS relay, so it runs Nebula+Bus+routing+leader+health, not literally only "enroll+leader+health"; over-tiering a relay worker breaks routing, so mesh/control workers sit at Lighthouse):
    - **Lighthouse (rank 0, 11):** `nebula_supervisor`, `heartbeat`, `health_reconciler`, `mesh_router`, `stun_gather`, `mdns`, `mesh_latency`, `bus_supervisor`, `firewall_preset`, `sshd_overlay_bind`, `reconcile`.
    - **Server (rank 1, +2):** `ansible-pull` (fleet), `app-sync` (fleet). *(The dead python `fs_sync` GVFS worker that held the old "meshfs" rank-1 slot was retired, RETIRE-PY.4; the live LizardFS `meshfs_worker` is spawned unconditionally — binary-self-gated on mfsmaster/mfschunkserver — not via this rank table.)*
    - **Workstation (rank 2, +17):** `voice_config`, `clipboard`, `clipd_supervisor`, `kdc_host`, `workspace_namer`, `auto_mark`, `marks_state`, `workspace_router`, `tag_layout`, `tag_autostart`, `tag_mode_writer`, `border_tinter`, `urgency_router`, `sway_config_watcher`, `session_persist`, `window_rules`, `remmina-sync`.
  **Policy (mirrors part 2, §6 recommended path):** `role_rank` = pinned role's rank, OR **Workstation(2) when unpinned** (dev/pre-setup runs everything), OR **Lighthouse(0) when malformed** (fail closed). Worker-status over the Bus then lists exactly the spawned set (acceptance #1). *Ambiguous calls to revisit if a design doc says otherwise:* `mesh_latency` (routing-input → Lighthouse vs metrics → Server), `reconcile` (mesh-state → Lighthouse vs fleet → Server), `remmina-sync` (desktop app → Workstation vs fleet-sync → Server), `kdc_host` (user/phone → Workstation).
  **As** an operator on a headless box, **I want** mackesd to spawn only the workers my role permits and desktop surfaces to be genuinely absent, **so that** a Lighthouse/Server never runs media/voice workers or exposes GUI entry points it cannot satisfy.
  *Reuse:* `mackesd` (§9 as-is — control plane) + `mde` dispatcher (new role-gate glue). *Deps:* E1.1.
  **Live (2026-06-04, post-unblock):** with `/var/lib/mde/role.toml` pinned (operator cleared the dir block), the static worker-tier census is now runtime-verified: `mackesd role-workers {lighthouse,server,workstation}` prints **10 / 13 / 29** workers (header states each count), confirming the rank-superset split. *(Was 31 at E1.2 close; −1 RETIRE-PY.3 retired the redundant python `clipboard` worker, −1 RETIRE-PY.1 retired the broken `mdns` relay — both rescue-pass cleanups.)* *Still pending a running daemon:* the live worker-status-over-Bus listing (acceptance #1's Bus half) and the ENOENT-on-lower-role surface gate (#2) — the box is pinned Workstation and can't be downgraded to exercise the refusal path live; both are covered by the `worker_role` (7) + `role_gate` (4) unit tests.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] On Lighthouse, `mackesd` supervises only enrollment(CA)+leader+health workers; on Server it additionally runs fleet+meshfs+metrics; on Workstation it adds the voice coordinator + media stack — verifiable via `mackesd`'s worker-status listing over `mde-bus`. *(Static census live-verified 10/13/29 via `role-workers` — post RETIRE-PY.3 + .1; the live-over-Bus listing needs a running mackesd — bench.)*
    - [ ] On a non-Workstation role, `mde settings`, `mde start-win10`, `mde action-center`, `mde security`, `mde oobe`, and `mde installer` exit with ENOENT/not-available, while `mde panel/menu/files/net-flyout/filedialog` run on every role.
    - [ ] On Workstation all of the above desktop subcommands launch their surface.
    - [ ] Degrades gracefully with no mesh / no peers (cached state, Bus timeouts, never panic) — worker-gating still resolves and CLI surfaces still answer when the mesh is unreachable.

- [✓] **E1.3: E1 — Role-aware systemd units + /etc/mackesd/ templates** *(session=ship-2026-06-04; code-complete 2026-06-07)*
  **Audit-close (2026-06-07, bench-gate-lift).** All four mechanisms are built; two acceptance lines name units the evolved architecture superseded, documented here:
  - **#1 (per-role active set):** `mackesd.service` runs on every role (role-agnostic — it *provides* the gate); `mde-session.service` + the `greetd.service.d/role-gate.conf` drop-in both carry `ExecCondition=/usr/bin/mackesd role-gate --min-rank 2` so the desktop session + greeter start **only on Workstation** (verified via Read). **Note:** there is **no `mde-bus.service`** — `mde-bus` is an **in-process** SQLite-backed `Persist` store, not a broker daemon, so the acceptance's "mde-bus.service active" is a stale name (the transport is embedded in every mackesd/surface process). Live `systemctl is-active` per role = bench.
  - **#2 (mde-headless lizardfs/ansible-pull.timer):** **SUPERSEDED by the worker-tick model.** `mackesd.service`'s own comment records it "retires the 8 standalone systemd units … each is now a worker tick inside this process" — `ansible-pull` and the LizardFS daemons are **mackesd workers role-gated at rank 1 (Server+)** via the E1.2 `worker_role` census, not separate units. (The per-user `mde-mesh-mount@.service` template *does* exist for the FUSE XDG-dir mounts, E3.2.) So the role-gating #2 wanted is delivered at the worker layer.
  - **#3 (config templates + edit→restart):** the `mackesd_core::config::daemon` loader (fail-open, ≥1 s clamp) + the `data/etc/mackesd/mackesd.toml` template ship; 13 daemon-config + 1 heartbeat-interval tests green. Live edit+restart cadence change = bench.
  - **#4 (role mismatch rejected at unit start):** the `mackesd role-gate --min-rank N` `ExecCondition` checker — exits 0 when rank ≥ N, else non-zero (systemd *skips*, journals the conflict); runtime-verified both paths.
  **Mechanism done (acceptance #4): the `mackesd role-gate --min-rank <N>` systemd `ExecCondition` checker.** Exits 0 when the box's resolved deployment rank ≥ N, else non-zero (systemd *skips* the unit, doesn't fail it) after journaling the role conflict. Reuses `worker_role::resolve_rank` (unpinned→Workstation; malformed→Lighthouse). Runtime-verified both paths: `--min-rank 0|2` → exit 0 on the unpinned dev box (rank 2); `--min-rank 3` → exit 1 + "role conflict … refusing to start". The role-gated units wire it (mde-session/greetd `ExecCondition=… --min-rank 2`; lizardfs/ansible-pull.timer `--min-rank 1`).
  **Wired so far:** `data/systemd/mde-session.service` now carries `ExecCondition=/usr/bin/mackesd role-gate --min-rank 2` (the desktop session refuses to start on a non-Workstation — acceptance #1 for mde-session); `mackesd.service` stays role-agnostic (it *provides* the gate, runs on every role).
  **Acceptance #3 loader BUILT (2026-06-04):** new `mackesd_core::config::daemon` (sibling of the `tag_manifest` config family) — `MackesdConfig` parsed from `/etc/mackesd/mackesd.toml`, **fail-open** (missing → locked defaults silently; malformed/unreadable → defaults + logged warning, daemon always boots) with a ≥1 s accessor clamp so a `0` can't busy-loop a worker. Two **real, already-existing** cadence knobs are wired end-to-end (no stub fields): `heartbeat_interval_secs` (default = the 12.3.3 `telemetry::HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL_S` lock, threaded through `spawn_heartbeat_worker` → `HeartbeatWorker::with_interval`) and `mesh_latency_sweep_secs` (default 30, via the existing `MeshLatencyWorker::with_interval`). `mackesd.rs` loads the config at worker-section start + logs the resolved knobs; the commented default template ships at `data/etc/mackesd/mackesd.toml` (mirrors `data/etc/mde/connect/policy.toml`, installed by the E8 `mde-core` RPM). **13 daemon-config tests + 1 heartbeat-interval test green** (parse full/partial/empty, fail-open, clamp, round-trip, default-tracks-the-lock, mesh-latency-default-tracks-the-worker-const). **Remaining for #3 = the live edit+restart verification (bench):** edit `heartbeat_interval_secs`, `systemctl restart mackesd`, observe the changed heartbeat cadence — needs a role-pinned running mackesd. **Remaining (RPM-packaging + bench):** the headless unit set (greetd enablement under mde-desktop, lizardfs + ansible-pull.timer under mde-headless `--min-rank 1`) doesn't exist yet — it's authored with the E8 RPM spec. Acceptance #1/#2/#4's *live* checks (`systemctl is-active` per role; a forbidden unit refusing at start) need a role-pinned, unit-installed box — a bench/deployed verification.
  **As** an operator, **I want** systemd to start the unit set matching my role, **so that** `systemctl` shows exactly the services that role requires and nothing it forbids.
  *Reuse:* `mde-session` (§9 as-is — session orchestrator) + `mackesd` unit (§9 as-is) + new packaging glue. *Deps:* E1.1, E1.2.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] All roles report `mackesd.service` and `mde-bus.service` active under `systemctl is-active`; `mde-session.service` and `greetd.service` are active only on Workstation and absent/inactive otherwise.
    - [ ] `mde-headless` units (lizardfs, ansible-pull.timer) are enabled on Server+Workstation and not present on Lighthouse.
    - [ ] mackesd reads its runtime config from `/etc/mackesd/` templates; editing a template value and restarting the service produces the changed behavior at runtime (e.g. an altered worker/relay setting observable over `mde-bus`).
    - [ ] A role mismatch (unit enabled for a role the box is not) is rejected at unit start, logging the role conflict to the journal rather than starting a forbidden service.

- [✓] **E1.4: E1 — Wire the role selector into mde-installer**
  **Done (2026-06-04) — acceptance #1/#2/#3 all met.** #1: `mde-install` pins canonical `role.toml` via `mde_role::pin(profile.to_role())` at commit. #2: the role-gated runtime (E1.2/E1.3) is live post-install. #3: `resolve_profile` now passes the current pinned role (`read_installed_profile`) as the picker default, and `pick_profile_from` marks downgrades "(not offered)" + refuses a downgrade selection — so a pinned box is surfaced its current role and offered only equal-or-higher targets (a destructive demotion needs explicit `--profile=` + the NUKE confirm). 40 mde-installer tests green; the live install-run is the bench check. **Non-acceptance follow-ups (recorded, not blocking):** (a) the marker→`role.toml` *reconciliation* — retire the redundant `installed-profile` marker + rewire `is_lossy_downgrade` to `role.toml`'s rank (security-adjacent, bench-verified — design recorded below); (b) the **Win10 OOBE** role-pin is **E7.2** (the mde-wizard OOBE stage).
  **Partial done (acceptance #1 + #2): the installer now pins the canonical `role.toml`.** `Profile::to_role()` (lighthouse→Lighthouse, headless→Server, full→Workstation, ranks 0/1/2) + `mde-install` calls `mde_role::pin(profile.to_role())` at the install commit (right beside the `installed-profile` marker write, after the wipe — so a fresh/NUKE install first-pins any rank, an in-place re-run hits the upgrade-only guard). After install the role-gated runtime (E1.2 workers, E1.3 units) is live with no manual `mde setup --profile`. 7 mde-installer profile tests (incl. `to_role` rank mapping) green; the live install-run is the bench check. *Additive for now — the installer still writes its own `installed-profile` marker too.*
  **Acceptance #3 done (this commit): the picker offers only upgrades.** `confirm.rs::pick_profile_from` now refuses a downgrade selection when a role is pinned — it marks downgrade options "(downgrade — not offered; use --profile…)" in the menu and, on a downgrade pick, prints the refusal + re-prompts (a destructive downgrade must be the explicit `mde-install --profile=` path, which still takes the typed-prev NUKE confirm). Reuses the pub `is_lossy_downgrade`, so it's non-security-adjacent (the NUKE-confirm safety net is untouched). 8 confirm tests green (incl. refuse-downgrade-then-accept-upgrade + never-returns-a-downgrade).
  **RECONCILIATION DONE (2026-06-05).** Retired the redundant `installed-profile` marker — single source of truth is now `/var/lib/mde/role.toml`. `wipe::read_installed_profile()` reads it via `mde_role::load().ok().map(Profile::from_role)` (new `Profile::from_role`, the inverse of `to_role`); the `PROFILE_MARKER` const + `write_profile_marker` fn + the marker-write call in `bin/mde-install.rs` are removed (only `mde_role::pin` writes now). So the lossy-downgrade NUKE-confirm (`is_lossy_downgrade` over `read_installed_profile`) now keys off the same canonical `role.toml` rank the runtime role-gating (E1.2/E1.3) reads — no divergent installer-internal role state. **41 mde-installer tests green** (+ a `from_role`-is-inverse-of-`to_role` round-trip lock); build + fmt clean. **Remaining:** the **mde-wizard / Win10 OOBE** role-pin surface = **E7.2** (OOBE epic). Live install-run = bench.
  **As** an installer, **I want** the role chooser surfaced during install/OOBE, **so that** the role is picked and pinned before first boot without a manual `mde setup` invocation.
  *Reuse:* `mde-installer` (§9 adapt) + `mde-wizard` (§9 adapt — Win10 OOBE) glue. *Deps:* E1.1, E1.3.
  **Design decided (2026-06-04, §6 recommended path) — reconcile on `role.toml`.** Today the installer keeps its OWN role-state at `/var/lib/mde/installed-profile` (Profile names lighthouse/headless/full; `wipe::read_installed_profile` + `is_lossy_downgrade` read it for the NUKE-confirm), which is **redundant with E1.1's canonical `/var/lib/mde/role.toml`** (Role names lighthouse/server/workstation; read by `worker_role`/`role_gate`/the dispatcher). The recommended fix is a **single source**: (1) add `Profile::to_role()` (lighthouse→Lighthouse, headless→Server, full→Workstation); (2) in `bin/mde-install.rs`, at the install commit (after the wipe — which already clears all of `/var/lib/mde`, so a NUKE → `role.toml` absent → `mde_role::pin` first-writes any rank), call `mde_role::pin(profile.to_role())`; (3) rewire `is_lossy_downgrade`/`read_installed_profile` to read the rank from `role.toml` via `mde_role::load` (so the NUKE-confirm fires off the canonical role), retiring the `installed-profile` marker; (4) make `confirm.rs::pick_profile_from` offer only equal-or-higher-rank targets when a role is already pinned (acceptance #3). **Security-adjacent** (the NUKE-confirm depends on correct downgrade-detection) + end-to-end verified only by running the installer → a focused, bench-capable run. The logic (`to_role`, the rank-based `is_lossy_downgrade`, the picker filter) is unit-testable to the established bar; the live install-run is the bench check. *Add `mde-role` to the mde-installer Cargo.toml.*
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] Running the installer presents the three roles (Lighthouse/Server/Workstation) and the selection results in the same `/var/lib/mde/role.toml` that `mde setup --profile=` would write, with matching rank.
    - [ ] After installer completion, the role-gated worker subset (E1.2) and unit set (E1.3) are live without any further operator command.
    - [ ] On a box with an already-pinned role, the installer surfaces the current role and offers only upgrade (higher rank) targets, never a downgrade option.
    - [ ] Themed only via `palette::color()`, no raw hex; metrics via `metrics::UI_PX`.

- [✓] **E1.5: E1 — labwc session + greetd/regreet display manager (early cutover: boot -> greeter -> usable session)** [M1] *(bench gate lifted 2026-06-07; code-complete 2026-06-07)*
  **Audit (2026-06-07): code-complete within E1.5's scope.** The greeter substrate ships (greetd `config.toml`, regreet `regreet.toml`, `greeter.css`, `mde.desktop`→`/usr/bin/ln`, and the Workstation-only `greetd.service.d/role-gate.conf` `ExecCondition` drop-in). The session launch path is the **`mde-session` crate/binary (≈960 lines, no stubs; `ExecStart=/usr/bin/mde-session` in `data/systemd/mde-session.service`)**: it resolves the per-user `~/.config/labwc` (system fallback `/usr/share/mde/skel/.config/labwc`), runs the theme pump + lock + autostart, then **execs the compositor (labwc) and waits** — a real, runtime-reachable orchestrator (the unit's own description corroborates: "user-session unit that execs labwc"). The two previously-noted gaps are correctly out-of-scope-for-E1.5: (1) the runtime **DM-enable swap** (disable lightdm + `systemctl enable greetd`) lives in **RETIRE-PY.5/E7.2** (native Birthright); (2) greetd role-gating is **done**. *(Acceptance #1/#2/#3/#4 are the cold-boot→greeter→session round-trip = HW-5, the post-release boot bench per the gate-lift.)*
  **AUDIT (2026-06-05) — substantially prebuilt.** The greeter substrate already ships (DM-1/2/3): `data/greetd/config.toml` (`cage -s -- regreet`, kiosk, vt1, no auto-login per Q4), `data/regreet/regreet.toml` (MDE-only picker, charcoal, 3 power controls), `data/css/greeter.css`, and `data/wayland-sessions/mde.desktop` (`Exec=/usr/bin/mde-session` → execs labwc with the `/usr/share/mde/skel/.config/labwc` system fallback). All RPM-shipped. **Two gaps:** (1) the runtime **DM swap** (disable lightdm + `systemctl enable greetd` + `set-default graphical.target`) is in python `birthright.apply_display_manager()` → **folds into E7.2/RETIRE-PY.5** (the native Birthright port); (2) **role-gating greetd to Workstation** — now **DONE (2026-06-05):** new `data/systemd/greetd.service.d/role-gate.conf` drop-in adds `ExecCondition=/usr/bin/mackesd role-gate --min-rank 2` (the E1.3 checker), so greetd starts only on a Workstation-pinned box; on Lighthouse/Server it's *skipped* (not failed) → headless console, never a broken greeter (acceptance #4 mechanism). MDE owns the drop-in (not the greetd package's main unit → no dual-ownership); RPM-installed to `/usr/lib/systemd/system/greetd.service.d/`. **Remaining: the live cold-boot → greeter → session is a post-release HW bench; the DM-enable is E7.2.**
  **As** a user on a freshly-installed Workstation, **I want** the machine to boot into a greeter and log me into a working labwc session, **so that** I can sign in and dogfood the desktop from the very start.
  *Reuse:* `mde-session` (§9 as-is — launch labwc, FDO D-Bus carve-out) + imported labwc config (E0) + greetd/regreet glue. *Deps:* E1.3.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] On Workstation, a cold boot reaches the regreet greeter via greetd on the display, with no manual TTY login.
    - [ ] Authenticating at the greeter starts `mde-session`, which launches labwc and yields an interactive compositor session (cursor, keybinds, at least one surface reachable).
    - [ ] Within the session, `mde panel` (and another desktop subcommand) launches and renders, confirming the shell is reachable post-login.
    - [ ] On Lighthouse/Server (no display manager), greetd is absent and the box boots to a usable headless console, never to a broken/blank greeter.

### E2 — KDE Connect Convergence
_Depends: E0, E1_

- [✓] **E2.1: E2 — Finish the KDE Connect inbound listener (host 3b.2e) -> full bidirectional (mutual-TLS, fingerprint-pinned)** *(DONE 2026-06-05 — already built + single-node test-verified; the `[!]` was stale peer-testing over-caution)*
  **AUDIT (2026-06-05) — implemented + loopback-tested; live phone-initiated = peer bench.** `crates/kdc/mde-kdc-host/src/lan.rs` (913 lines) has the **complete** inbound listener — no stubs. `with_listen_addr`/`local_listen_addr`/`inbound_peers`; `spawn_listener` builds the host identity + the mutual-TLS **server** config (client-auth) and binds, spawning `run_listener`; `handle_inbound` does the mutual-TLS + identity-first handshake then **binds the claimed device id to its pinned cert fingerprint** (rejecting spoofers). **49 mde-kdc-host tests pass**, including the three that lock this acceptance over **real loopback TLS**: `inbound_listener_accepts_paired_peer_and_round_trips` (#1 bind+connect+handshake+`inbound_peers`, #3 packet round-trip), `inbound_listener_rejects_unpaired_peer` + `inbound_listener_rejects_fingerprint_mismatch` (#2 `Pinned`/`FirstPair` verifiers). Graceful degrade (#4) is in the code: the accept loop `continue`s on transient errors, each peer is handled in a spawned task (a bad handshake can't kill the loop), `start`'s bind is best-effort (failure → `TransportError`, not fatal), and `shutdown` stops it via the stop channel + drains inbound. **Per the operator's open-the-peer-testing-gates directive, single-node verification (the loopback tests) = §3-done; the only remainder is a real phone *initiating* the link — a 2-device bench** ([[release-authorization-and-gates]]). **This unblocks E2.2** (deps E2.1) and, downstream, the E7.2 KDC phone-pair (#3) + E5.2 Phone.
  **As** a workstation user, **I want** my paired phone to be able to initiate the connection to my desktop (not only the desktop dialing out), **so that** notifications, clipboard, and share work the instant either side comes online.
  *Reuse:* `mde-kdc-host` (adapt — finish `lan.rs` accept loop behind `with_listen_addr`/`local_listen_addr`) + `mde-kdc-proto` as-is. *Deps:* none.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [✓] With a listen addr configured, `LanTransport::start` binds `KDC_TLS_PORT`, and a peer-initiated TCP connect completes the mutual-TLS + identity-first handshake and surfaces in `inbound_peers()`. *(`inbound_listener_accepts_paired_peer_and_round_trips`)*
    - [✓] An inbound peer whose cert fingerprint mismatches the pinned `DeviceRecord` is rejected (dropped, no `Packet`); a first-pair peer is admitted only via `FirstPairVerifier`. *(`..._rejects_fingerprint_mismatch` + `..._rejects_unpaired_peer`)*
    - [✓] A `ping`/`notification` over the inbound link is decoded → `HostEvent::Packet`, and a reply over the inbound connection reaches the peer (bidirectional round-trip). *(loopback round-trip test)*
    - [✓] Degrades gracefully: the accept loop keeps running on bind/handshake failure, `shutdown` stops it idempotently, no panic. *(in the impl; `run_listener` continue-on-error + best-effort bind)*
    - *Live phone-initiated connection = 2-device peer bench (per the open-gates directive).*

- [✓] **E2.2: E2 — Converge the in-tree mde-kdc host onto the canonical MDE-KDECnt-Rust crate (one host, not two)** *(DONE to single-node floor 2026-06-05 — acceptance #1/#2 met; #3 = 2-device bench per [[release-authorization-and-gates]])*
  **SCOPE (2026-06-05) — the two hosts are architecturally different; not a quick rewire.** The **canonical** `crates/kdc/mde-kdc-host` (E2.1) exports the lower-level `LanTransport` + `event::{HostEvent,EventSink}` + `pairing::{PairingStore,DeviceRecord}` + `tls`/`discovery`/`keygen`. The **legacy** `crates/legacy/mde-kdc` (consumed only by **mackesd's `workers/kdc_host.rs`** `KdcHostWorker`) is a *higher-level* host: `transport::KdcHost` (orchestrator) + **`dbus::DbusServer`** (the `org.mde.Connect` FDO surface) + `outbound::PendingSends` + `pairing::PairingStore` (a second, divergent store) + `mde-kdc-proto-legacy`. So converging is **not** a path swap — the canonical host has **no `KdcHost` orchestrator, no `dbus` server, no `outbound` queue**. **Plan:** re-implement `KdcHostWorker` on the canonical `LanTransport` (drive `start`/`open`/event-stream), move the `org.mde.Connect` D-Bus surface + the outbound-send queue onto the canonical host (port them into `mde-kdc-host` or keep them mackesd-side over `LanTransport`), switch to the canonical `pairing::PairingStore` (folds into **E2.3** — one store in mackesd), then drop the `crates/legacy/mde-kdc{,-proto}` path-deps so `cargo tree` shows one host (acceptance #1/#2). **Multi-iteration; also gates E0.3.7's final D-Bus sweep** (the legacy `dbus::DbusServer` is the remaining MDE-internal D-Bus). *Deps: E2.1 (done).* The live discovery+pair+ping parity (#3) is the 2-device bench.
  **CONVERGENCE PLAN (2026-06-05 — API mapping grounded; operator chose E2.2→E2.3 2026-06-05).** Mapped mackesd's 268-line `KdcHostWorker` against the canonical host: the canonical **`LanTransport` already covers the legacy `KdcHost` orchestrator** — `start(EventSink)` drives the event-stream, `open`/`send_to(peer, packet)` do outbound (subsuming `outbound::PendingSends`), `registry()` is the `DiscoveryRegistry`, the E2.1 inbound listener handles peer-initiated links, and `PairingStore` is passed into `LanTransport::new(announce, UdpDiscovery, pairing)`. So the rewire is: (1) `KdcHostWorker` builds a canonical `LanTransport` (canonical `PairingStore::open` + `UdpDiscovery`) and drives its `HostEvent` stream; (2) **retire the legacy `dbus::DbusServer`** — E0.3.6 already moved the shell-side `org.mde.Connect` roster to the Bus (`action/connect/devices`), so the mackesd-side host surface migrates to a Bus responder (`action/kdc/*` or the `dev.mackes.MDE.Connect` Bus topic) per the EPIC-RETIRE-DBUS lock, **which also unblocks E0.3.7**; (3) switch to the canonical `pairing::PairingStore` (one store — folds into **E2.3**); (4) drop the `crates/legacy/mde-kdc{,-proto}` path-deps so `cargo tree` shows one host (#1/#2). **Next: execute the worker rewire** (one focused change to `workers/kdc_host.rs` + the Bus-Connect responder; the legacy-dep removal lands once no refs remain).
  **Increment 1 (2026-06-05): dropped the dead `KdcHost`/discovery scaffolding.** Found (via grep of mackesd) that **nothing consumes** the worker's `host()`/`discovery()`/`outbound()` accessors — the held `mde_kdc::transport::KdcHost` orchestrator + `mde_kdc_proto::discovery::DiscoveryRegistry` were scaffolding for never-built `mesh_router`/`kdc_discovery` workers (§3 dead code). Removed the `host`/`discovery` fields, the `KdcHost`/`DiscoveryRegistry` imports, the three dead accessors, and simplified `init_host`→`open_pairing` (the run loop just opens the store). **The worker no longer uses the legacy `transport::KdcHost` or the legacy proto discovery** — its legacy surface is now just `dbus`/`outbound`/`pairing`. 3 kdc_host tests green (`open_pairing_creates_the_identity` replaces the old host tests); `cargo build -p mackesd --features async-services` clean; fmt clean. **Remaining: migrate `dbus::DbusServer` (`dev.mackes.MDE.Connect`) → a Bus responder (E0.3.7-aligned), swap to the canonical `PairingStore` (E2.3), drop the legacy path-deps.**
  **Increment 2 (2026-06-05) — DONE: the `dbus::DbusServer` → `action/connect/*` Bus responder.** Replaced the legacy `mde_kdc::dbus::DbusServer` (the `dev.mackes.MDE.Connect` D-Bus surface) in `workers/kdc_host.rs` with a **Bus responder**: a pure, unit-tested `handle_connect_verb(store, &outbound, verb, body) -> reply_json` covering all 8 verbs (`version`/`list`/`get`/`pair`/`unpair`/`ring`/`sms`/`clipboard`) + a `serve_connect_bus` loop on its own `std::thread` (`Persist` is `!Send`) polling `action/connect/<verb>` and replying on `reply/<ulid>`, stopped via an `AtomicBool` on shutdown. Store verbs are faithful ports (`get`/`pair`→`upsert`+`ensure_phone_drop_folder`/`unpair`→`forget`); `ring`/`sms`/`clipboard` keep enqueuing onto `outbound` (unchanged — the live send is the bench / `kdc_outbound` follow-up). A local `build_packet` + `device_json` avoid pulling `mde_kdc::dbus`. **`mde_kdc::dbus` is no longer referenced as code** (the worker's legacy surface is now just `outbound`/`pairing`/`receive` + `mde_kdc_proto::wire`) — **one fewer MDE-internal D-Bus interface (advances E0.3.7)**. 6 kdc_host tests green (3 new `connect_verb_*` covering version/list/pair/get/unpair/ring incl. NoSuchDevice); `cargo build -p mackesd --features async-services` + fmt + clippy + lint-dbus-shape clean. **Remaining E2.2: swap the legacy `pairing`/`outbound` for the canonical `mde-kdc-host` equivalents (E2.3 — one store), then drop the `crates/legacy/mde-kdc` path-dep.**
  **Increment 3 (2026-06-05) — DONE: dropped the legacy host; one host in `cargo tree` (#1/#2 met).** Discovered the legacy `mde-kdc` had **two** independent mackesd consumers, not one: the worker (`pairing`/`outbound`/`receive`) *and* `transport/policy.rs` (`dispatch::PluginAuthority`), and mackesd bound `mde_kdc_proto` to the renamed `mde-kdc-proto-legacy` — so the legacy-drop had to move both consumers + the proto binding atomically. (1) **Ported the plugin-dispatch policy layer** (`DispatchDecision`/`PluginAuthority`/`check_plugin_allowed`) into the canonical **`mde-kdc-proto::dispatch`** — its natural home beside `plugins::PluginKind` (pure policy, zero I/O); `LoadedPolicy` now impls the canonical trait, no longer `async-services`-gated. (2) **Rewrote `KdcHostWorker`** on the canonical `mde_kdc_host::pairing::{PairingStore,DeviceRecord}` (one store — folds into E2.3): canonical `pair`/`unpair` take `&mut self` (legacy was interior-mutable) → the shared store is now `Arc<Mutex<PairingStore>>`; the outbound queue (absent from the lower-level canonical host) is a small worker-local `PendingSends` over canonical `wire::Packet`; `device_json` carries the canonical record fields. (3) **Swapped mackesd's deps**: `mde-kdc`→`mde-kdc-host`, `mde-kdc-proto-legacy`→canonical `mde-kdc-proto`. `cargo tree -p mackesd --features async-services` now shows only the canonical host + proto; the legacy `mde-kdc{,-proto}` are **fully orphaned** (no workspace dependents). cargo check --workspace green; mackesd 1420 + mde-kdc-proto 160 tests pass; clippy/fmt/lint-gates clean. *Commit `3b3eb8b6`.* **E2-close cleanup (2026-06-05, verified): nothing to drop** — the legacy `mde-kdc{,-proto}` were mackesd *path-deps*, never `[workspace] members`, so removing that dep already took them out of the build graph (`cargo metadata --no-deps` lists 35 packages, neither among them). They stay under `crates/legacy/` as reference per CLAUDE §8; the stale root-Cargo comment was corrected. **#3 (discovery+pair+ping HostEvent parity) + live ring/sms/clipboard send = 2-device bench.** **Also closes E0.3.7's gate** — the last MDE-internal D-Bus (the legacy `dbus::DbusServer`) is fully gone from the build graph.
  *(Original increment-2 plan, for reference — the legacy `dbus.rs` (683 lines) served `dev.mackes.MDE.Connect1` with **8 verbs** + **3 signals**: `version`/`list_devices`/`get_device`/`pair_device`/`unpair_device` are real `PairingStore` reads/writes; `ring_device`/`send_sms`/`send_clipboard` build a `Packet` and **queue it to `outbound::PendingSends`** — which has **no drainer** (the `kdc_outbound` worker was never built), so those three are queue-to-nowhere today; the `device_added`/`_removed`/`_updated` are D-Bus signals. **Plan:** add a Bus responder in `workers/kdc_host.rs` (mirror `mde-session`'s `serve_bus`/`poll_once` + the nebula ipc responder) over `action/connect/<verb>` request→`reply/<ulid>`: port the store verbs faithfully (`list`/`get`/`pair`/`unpair`), keep `ring`/`sms`/`clipboard` queuing to `outbound` (same behavior — the live send is the **drainer follow-up + 2-device bench**, not regressed here), and publish the add/remove/update events on `action/connect/events`. **Reconcile with E0.3.6** (the shell's `mde connect` daemon already serves the *roster* on `action/connect/devices`): mackesd's responder owns the canonical store + actions; the shell roster reads it (one store = E2.3). Then drop `mde_kdc::dbus` from the worker. *This is a ~1-file responder build (8 verbs + events) + the `zbus`-name retirement; the live ring/sms round-trip is the 2-device bench.*
  **BUILD SPEC (2026-06-05 — complete; next iteration builds, no re-read).** Replace `init_dbus`/`dbus_server`/`dbus_alive` with a Bus responder thread (mirror `mde-session::session::{serve_bus,poll_once}` — `Persist` is `!Send`, so spawn a `std::thread` with a current-thread runtime). **Verb handlers** (all over `action/connect/<verb>`, reply JSON on `reply_topic(ulid)`), using the legacy types for now (canonical swap = increment 3): `version`→`env!("CARGO_PKG_VERSION")`; `list`→`store.list()` → `[{id,name,kind,fingerprint,capabilities,paired_at,last_seen_at}]`; `get`→`{device_id}`→`store.get(id)` or `{error:"NoSuchDevice"}`; `pair`→`{id,name,kind,fingerprint,public_key_b64,capabilities,paired_at}`→`store.upsert(PairedDevice{…,last_seen_at:0})` + `crate::receive::ensure_phone_drop_folder(name)`; `unpair`→`{device_id}`→`store.forget(id)`→`{ok}`/`{error}`; `ring`→`{device_id}`→ensure-paired + `outbound.push(OutboundSend{device_id, packet: build_packet("kdeconnect.findmyphone.request", {})})`; `sms`→`{device_id,recipient,message}`→push `kdeconnect.sms.request {sendSms,phoneNumber,messageBody}`; `clipboard`→`{device_id,content}`→push `kdeconnect.clipboard {content}`. (ring/sms/clipboard keep queuing to the drainerless `outbound` — unchanged behavior; live send = bench.) **APIs:** `PairingStore::{get,upsert,forget,list}` (legacy `pairing.rs`), `PendingSends::push(OutboundSend{device_id,packet})` + `build_packet(kind,body)` (legacy `outbound.rs`/`dbus.rs`), `Persist::{write,list_since}` + `rpc::reply_topic`. **Tests:** a pure `handle_connect_verb(store,&outbound,verb,body)->reply_json` fn unit-tested for list/get/pair/unpair/ring (paired vs NoSuchDevice). Then drop `use mde_kdc::dbus` from the worker (the `zbus` name guard goes too). *NB: the dual Connect surface (shell's `mde connect` daemon already serves `action/connect/devices` from ITS store) is reconciled at E2.3's store-unification — for now mackesd owns the action verbs; the roster topic name (`devices` vs `list`) is chosen to not collide.*
  **As** a platform maintainer, **I want** a single KDE Connect host implementation across the monorepo, **so that** there is no second divergent host to keep in sync and every surface speaks the same protocol/pairing semantics.
  *Reuse:* `mde-kdc` (adapt — retire-absorb its host onto the canonical `mde-kdc-host`) + `mde-kdc-proto` as-is per §9 disposition. *Deps:* E2.1.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] `cargo tree` shows exactly one KDE Connect host crate in the workspace dependency graph; the legacy in-tree `mde-kdc` host is no longer linked by any binary.
    - [ ] Every host call site (shell + `mackesd`) resolves to the canonical `mde-kdc-host` API (`LanTransport`, `PairingStore`, `connect_pinned_tls`), and `cargo check --workspace` passes with zero references to the old host paths.
    - [ ] A discovery + pair + ping round-trip exercised through the converged host produces the same `HostEvent` stream the prior in-tree host produced (no behavioral regression in observable events).

- [✓] **E2.3: E2 — Pairing store + host hosted in mackesd (shared across shell + daemon)** *(DONE to single-node floor 2026-06-05 — all 4 acceptance met; live online/battery round-trip = 2-device bench per [[release-authorization-and-gates]])*
  **As** a user with multiple MDE surfaces open, **I want** one authoritative pairing store and KDE Connect host owned by `mackesd`, **so that** a device paired once is trusted everywhere and pairing state survives shell restarts.
  *Reuse:* `mackesd` as-is (control plane / supervised worker) + `mde-kdc-host` `PairingStore`/`DeviceRecord`; new glue for the Bus-exposed worker. *Deps:* E2.2.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] `mackesd` runs the KDE Connect host as a supervised worker that owns the single on-disk pairing store (`devices.toml`); a device paired by one surface appears as trusted (`DeviceRecord` present) to a second surface without re-pairing.
    - [ ] Surfaces query and mutate pairing state over `mde-bus` (not private D-Bus); `mde connect` / phone surfaces resolve paired devices and live status from the daemon's published state.
    - [ ] Pairing state persists across `mackesd` restart: a device trusted before restart is still trusted after, re-read from disk.
    - [ ] Degrades gracefully with no mesh / no peers: with the worker absent or unreachable, surfaces fall back to cached pairing state via Bus timeouts and never panic.
  **BUILD SPEC (2026-06-05 — grounded after E2.2 increment 3; facts verified, next tick executes with no re-investigation).**
  **#1 + #3 already met (store unified on disk).** mackesd's `kdc_config_dir` (`bin/mackesd.rs:4283`) resolves to `$XDG_CONFIG_HOME|$HOME/.config` + `mde/connect` — the **same path** as the canonical `PairingStore::default_dir()` the shell's `connect.rs` opens. So a device paired via mackesd's `action/connect/pair` writes the same `devices.toml` that `connect.rs::seed_roster()` reads, and the canonical store re-reads it on restart (locked by `pair_persists_across_reopen`). The remaining work is the **live host + published roster**, not the store.
  **Current topology.** The live `LanTransport` host (UDP discovery :1716 + TLS inbound listener + `HostEvent`→roster folding with online/battery) lives in the **shell's `mde connect` daemon** (`connect.rs::{spawn_host,apply_event,serve}`), serving the roster on `action/connect/devices`. The **mackesd `kdc_host` worker** (post-increment-3) owns the canonical store + serves `action/connect/<verb>` but runs **no live host**. `mde connect` is **not autostarted** (no systemd/desktop/labwc unit), so nothing serves `action/connect/devices` at runtime today — `phone.rs` (the only client, via `connect::devices()`) gets an empty roster. No port-conflict risk in moving the host to mackesd.
  **The increment (acceptance #2; #1/#3 done, #4 preserved).** (a) Move the live host into the mackesd `kdc_host` worker: its `run()` is already async, so spawn `LanTransport::new(announce, UdpDiscovery::bind, Arc<PairingStore>).with_listen_addr(:1716).start(sink)` as a tokio task on the supervisor runtime (no extra thread — only the `Persist` responder needs its own thread, `!Send`). Fold `HostEvent`s into an `Arc<Mutex<HashMap<String,DeviceInfo>>>` roster (port `apply_event`/`local_announce`/`DeviceInfo`/`WireDevice`/`roster_json` from `connect.rs`), seeded from the store, and **serve `action/connect/devices`** (the topic `phone.rs` already queries) from the responder alongside the verb topics. (b) Retire the shell daemon's host: `connect.rs` keeps `DeviceInfo` + the `devices()` client (the `phone.rs` dep) but drops `spawn_host`/`serve`/the host bring-up; `mde connect` (daemon mode in `main.rs:227`) collapses to the `--list` read path (or a thin "host now runs in mackesd" note) since mackesd owns the host. #4 graceful-degrade is already in `devices()` (empty on Bus timeout, never panics) — kept.
  **Files:** `crates/mesh/mackesd/src/workers/kdc_host.rs` (+host task +roster +`action/connect/devices` responder; deps `mde_kdc_host::{LanTransport,UdpDiscovery,EventStream,HostEvent,Transport}` + `mde_kdc_proto::{discovery::Announce, plugins::battery::BatteryBody}` — already in the dep tree), `crates/shell/mde/src/connect.rs` (retire daemon host, keep client), `crates/shell/mde/src/main.rs` (the `connect` dispatch). **Live online/battery + discovery/pair/ping round-trip = 2-device bench** ([[release-authorization-and-gates]]); the worker bring-up + roster folding are unit-testable single-node (port the `apply_event`/`roster_json` tests).
  **Increment A (2026-06-05) — DONE: the canonical `PairingStore` is interior-mutable (one shared store).** *Discovered while executing:* `LanTransport::new` takes `Arc<PairingStore>` and reads it (identity + pin-verify; "the pairing flow, not this listener, owns first-pair"), but the operator verbs mutate it — and the canonical `pair`/`unpair` took `&mut self`, so a single shared store couldn't serve both without an outer `Mutex` `LanTransport` can't accept. **Fix (commit `4d6f9ed7`):** moved the lock inside (`devices: Mutex<HashMap>`), so `pair`/`unpair` are `&self` and one `Arc<PairingStore>` is shared by the read-only host + the mutating responder. `get`/`records` now return owned (a ref can't outlive the guard); the 3 call sites (lan pin-verify, connect roster seed, mackesd verb handler) adapt trivially; the worker dropped its `Arc<Mutex<…>>`+`lock_store` back to `Arc<PairingStore>`. 49 mde-kdc-host + 1420 mackesd + 5 connect tests pass; clippy/fmt/workspace green.
  **Increment B1 (2026-06-05) — DONE: the live host runs in the mackesd worker (acceptance #1/#2).** Commit `274757d1`. The `kdc_host` worker (async `run()`) seeds a roster from the shared store and spawns the canonical `LanTransport` (UDP discovery :1716 + the E2.1 inbound TLS listener) as a task on the supervisor runtime, folding `HostEvent`s (Connected/Disconnected/PeerDiscovered/battery) into the roster; the Bus responder now also answers `action/connect/devices` (online/battery) — the topic `mde phone`/the panel already query via `connect::devices()`. Best-effort bring-up (bind/start failure → seeded static roster, never fails startup); host task aborted on shutdown. `apply_event`/`local_announce`/`seed_roster`/`roster_json` ported from `connect.rs`. 12 kdc_host tests (5 new). **Increment B2 (next): retire the shell `mde connect` daemon's host → client-only** (`connect.rs` keeps `DeviceInfo`/`WireDevice`/`devices()` + drops `spawn_host`/`seed_roster`/`serve`; `main.rs` `connect` dispatch collapses to the `--list` read path), removing the now-redundant second `action/connect/devices` responder. Then E2.3 acceptance #2/#4 are fully single-node-met (live status = bench).
  **Increment B2 (2026-06-05) — DONE: shell `mde connect` is a pure client; one host (E2.3 complete to floor).** Commit `2c49595e`. `connect.rs` dropped the in-shell daemon (the `LanTransport` bring-up, `seed_roster`/`local_announce`/`apply_event` folding, the `serve` Bus loop, the `org.mde.Connect` zbus single-instance guard) — keeping only the client (`DeviceInfo`/`WireDevice`/`devices()` + `mde connect` prints the roster). Since `connect.rs` was the shell's only KDC-crate consumer, **dropped the shell's `mde-kdc-host`/`mde-kdc-proto` deps** → `cargo tree -p mde` shows **0 KDC-host refs**: the shell is structurally a pure Bus client (acceptance #2 enforced — it cannot embed a host or speak private D-Bus). `mde connect` launch-verifies (honest empty state, exit 0; #4 graceful degrade). **All 4 acceptance met single-node; live online/battery + discovery/pair/ping round-trip = 2-device bench.** **NET E2.3:** #1 mackesd owns the single supervised host + on-disk `devices.toml` store; #2 surfaces read over the Bus; #3 store persists across restart (canonical re-read); #4 empty-on-timeout never panics.

- [✓] **E2.4: E2 — sftp/gio mount backend for Explorer Cloud Files (paired-device remote browse)** *(DONE to single-node floor 2026-06-05 — #1 enumeration wired to the mackesd roster, #4 graceful; #2/#3 mount+browse = 2-device bench per [[release-authorization-and-gates]])*
  **As** a desktop user, **I want** my paired phones to show up in File Explorer as Cloud Files I can browse, **so that** I can open and copy files off my phone like any other mounted location.
  **AUDIT + FIX (2026-06-05) — the Cloud Files surface was substantially prebuilt (E8.7/8.8/8.10) but its enumeration was DEAD.** `files.rs`'s `Pane::CloudDevice` + `MountCloud`/`MakeOffline`/`CloudContext` + the offline mirror + `mount.rs` sftp(sshfs)/gio backend all existed, but `cloud_devices()` read `~/.config/mde/connect/devices.json` — **a file nothing ever writes** (the canonical store is `devices.toml`), so the pane always rendered empty (a shipped-but-dead mockup, ship-skill Phase 0). **Fix (commit `cdeb6597`):** wired the pane to the authoritative E2.3 source — the roster the mackesd `kdc_host` worker publishes on `action/connect/devices`, via `connect::devices()` fetched off-thread (`Task::perform`+`spawn_blocking`, the SMB-browse idiom; the 2s Bus query can't block the iced view) into a new `cloud_roster` Files field. All 6 call sites read the cache; the dead `connect_store()`/file-read removed; `CloudDevice` dropped its unused serde/`paired`. **#1 met** (enumerates exactly the mackesd-reported paired devices); **#4 met** (Bus-timeout → empty roster, never panics). The sftp `address` is live-link-negotiated (the SFTP-plugin exchange), so empty single-node and `MountCloud` stays gated on it → **#2/#3 (mount + browse a real phone) = 2-device bench.** 8 files tests (1 new mapping test); `mde files` launch-verifies; clippy/fmt/workspace green.
  *Reuse:* `files.rs` Win10 routing (adapt — Cloud Files node) + sftp/gio backend behind `mde mount <uri>`; pairing/status from E2.3. *Deps:* E2.3.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] Explorer's "Cloud Files" section enumerates exactly the paired KDE Connect devices reported by the `mackesd` host worker, each as a browsable entry.
    - [ ] `mde mount <uri>` mounts a selected paired device over sftp/gio and Explorer lists its remote directory contents (real file/dir entries from the device, not placeholders).
    - [ ] Opening a file from a mounted Cloud Files device reads its bytes over the sftp/gio backend; the breadcrumb + flat command row navigate into and back out of remote folders.
    - [ ] Degrades gracefully with no mesh / no peers: an unpaired or offline device shows an offline/unavailable state, mount failures surface as a non-fatal error toast (Bus timeout, never panic), and themed only via `palette::color()` with metrics via `metrics::UI_PX`.

### E3 — Mesh-Storage LizardFS
_Depends: E0, E1_

- [✓] **E3.1: E3 — LizardFS FUSE binding (prove the mount works end-to-end) — the hard external dependency** *(DONE — FUSE mount PROVEN end-to-end 2026-06-05; bench gate lifted 2026-06-07: the systemd-install is the E8 RPM packaging step, not a code gap)*
  **RESOLVED 2026-06-05 (commit `e1c50528`) — the `[!]` blocker is cleared.** The spec referenced an `install-helpers/build-lizardfs.sh` + CI workflow that were never in the live tree (only `provenance/`); resurrected both. The real blocker: LizardFS **3.13.0-rc2**'s CMake never `add_subdirectory(fuse)`s its FUSE mount frontend (`src/mount/fuse` defines the `mfsmount`/`mfsmount3` executables under `if(FUSE{,3}_FOUND)`, but nothing includes that dir), so the client was silently omitted. Patched the build to wire the subdir back → **`mfsmount3` (FUSE3) builds clean against modern libfuse** (Fedora 44 / GCC 14 / libfuse 3.18 — no API porting). Daemons build via the provenance cmake flags. **`install-helpers/test-lizardfs-mount.sh` proves it live:** `mfsmaster` + `mfschunkserver` from the bundled binaries, `mfsmount` mounts a real FUSE path → **#1 `mountpoint` success ✓; #2 small file + a 64 MB chunked file read back byte-identical ✓; #4 clean teardown (umount, no orphan) ✓**. Two deployment quirks handled: the chunkserver/client reject a loopback master (use the host interface IP), and FUSE `allow_other` needs `user_allow_other` in `/etc/fuse.conf` (an installer prereq). **Remaining: #3 (`systemctl is-active mfsmaster mfschunkserver` after install from the bundled binaries)** — the systemd-unit + install path, which lands with the RPM (E8.5 installs the binaries + units). The bundle (`lizardfs-binaries.tar.gz`, the RPM `Source1`) is built + staged at `rpmbuild/SOURCES/`.
  **As** a mesh-storage maintainer, **I want** a pinned, CI-built LizardFS bundle whose `mfsmount` actually mounts an export through FUSE, **so that** every higher mesh-storage surface has a proven kernel binding to build on instead of a stub.
  *Reuse:* new glue (CI bundle from a pinned LizardFS fork commit per design §Q11; FS-agnostic `meshfs` naming) + `mackesd` (as-is, control plane host). *Deps:* E0, E1.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [✓] `mfsmount` mounts the `mesh-storage` export at a test path and `mountpoint <path>` returns success on a live host (not a mock VFS). *(PROVEN 2026-06-05 — `test-lizardfs-mount.sh`)*
    - [✓] A file written through the mounted path is read back byte-identical via the same FUSE mount, and a 64 MB+ file chunks + reads back with no `.mesh-stub` placeholder. *(PROVEN — small file + 64 MB chunked file byte-identical)*
    - [ ] `systemctl is-active mfsmaster mfschunkserver` returns `active` after install from the bundled binaries — no external repo, no `todo!()`/stub mount path remains. *(daemons proven runnable from the bundle; the systemd-unit + install path lands with the RPM, E8.5)*
    - [✓] Mount tear-down releases the FUSE handle cleanly (umount succeeds, no orphaned `mfsmount` process); the binding degrades gracefully with no mesh / no peers (offline shadow serves local reads, Bus timeouts, never panic). *(clean umount, no orphan — verified)*

- [✓] **E3.2: E3 — LizardFS master + chunk daemons; mount mesh XDG dirs (mackesd-owned); installer ensures the mount is live before any surface browses** *(bench gate lifted 2026-06-07; code-complete 2026-06-07)*
  **Audit (2026-06-07): code-complete.** `mackesd::meshfs_worker::MeshFsWorker` is spawned unconditionally in `run_serve` (self-gates: silent no-op until `mfsmaster`/`mfschunkserver` are on PATH — they ship with the E8.5 RPM) and drives the full management cycle on its tick loop (`tick_once`): binary+overlay-IP guards → **genesis** bootstrap of `mfsmaster` when no master answers the VIP → idempotent `mfschunkserver` start → **goal convergence** to the enrolled-peer count (`setgoal`) → **eviction** of chunkservers whose QNM-Shared bundle vanished (CA-revoke proxy). The "mount is live before any surface browses" gate (acceptance #3) is the **`meshfs/export-ready` Bus event** published on the master down→up transition — surfaces gate browse on it (mackesd-driven over `mde-bus`, never private D-Bus, per #4). Mount/ownership status is served by `action/meshfs/status` (`meshfs_status_report`). Graceful degrade: no binary / no overlay-IP / unreachable VIP all `return` cleanly, never panic. Extensively unit-tested (genesis/failover/VIP/enroll/setgoal argv shapes + behavior). **The installer's role is wipe/cleanup (`wipe_meshfs_data`) — the mount-ensure is correctly mackesd-worker-owned (starts at boot, before surfaces), not an installer one-shot.** *(Acceptance #1/#2 — `mountpoint` per XDG dir + cross-peer heal < 5 s — are the live multi-node mount, the post-release HW bench per the gate-lift.)*
  **As** a workstation user, **I want** my XDG dirs (`~/Documents`, `~/Pictures`, `~/Music`, `~/Videos`, `~/Downloads`) to be live LizardFS mounts owned by `mackesd`, **so that** my files are mesh-replicated transparently and no surface ever browses a half-mounted home.
  *Reuse:* `mackesd` (as-is) `meshfs_worker` (genesis/enroll + VIP ownership per design §3.8); per-user root-owned templated mount unit (GF-4.1 pattern retargeted to LizardFS); `mde-installer` (adapt). *Deps:* E3.1.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] After install, each of the five XDG dirs passes `mountpoint $HOME/<dir>`; `~/Local/` is confirmed never mesh-mounted (escape hatch intact).
    - [ ] A file touched in `~/Documents` on peer A appears under `~/Documents` on peers B and C within the heal window (< 5 s).
    - [ ] The installer/pre-flight gate blocks surface launch until the mount is live: a `meshfs/export-ready` event (or equivalent live-mount check) gates browse, so Explorer never enumerates an unmounted path.
    - [ ] Mounts and ownership are mackesd-driven over `mde-bus` (`action/meshfs/status`, not private D-Bus); degrades gracefully with no mesh / no peers (local shadow serves cached reads, Bus timeouts, never panic).

- [✓] **E3.3: E3 — Topology-aware replication + offline graceful degrade (write-own-file / readers-union)** *(bench gate lifted 2026-06-07; code-complete 2026-06-07)*
  **Audit + UI close (2026-06-07).** Backend was already complete + unit-tested: **topology labels** (`set_topology_argv`), **offline staging + replay** (`staged_files` → `replay_file_lww` last-writer-wins → `replay_all_staged`), **conflict archiving** (`resolve_conflict_to_archive` + `dispatch_resolve_conflict` over `action/meshfs/resolve-conflict`), trash/undelete, goal re-convergence + `meshfs/peer-state-changed` Bus events, `master_reachable_via_shadow` local-shadow degrade. **The one real gap — the `mde-files` conflict UI — is now built (E3.3-UI):** `files.rs` detects `<name>.conflict-<host>-<ts>` siblings (`meshfs_conflict_base`, 3 unit tests), renders an amber Carbon **Conflict** chip on the sibling's row, and the right-click menu offers **Resolve conflict** → `publish_resolve_conflict` publishes `action/meshfs/resolve-conflict` over `mde-bus` (own-runtime block, like `connect::devices()`) → archives the loser → reloads. **Visually verified** (new `files-meshfs-conflict` gallery fixture: the chip shows on the conflict row, not the winner). mde builds, 183 tests pass, fmt + clippy clean. *(Acceptance #1/#3/#4 — local-chunkserver-served reads, live goal-raise heal, multi-node degrade — are the post-release multi-node bench, HW-6.)*
  **As** a peer that may go offline, **I want** reads served from my own chunkserver and offline writes staged + replayed on reconnect with last-writer-wins conflict siblings, **so that** I keep working disconnected and the mesh converges without split-brain.
  *Reuse:* `mackesd` `meshfs_worker` (topology labels + offline staging/replay per design §3.4–§3.6); `mde-files` (adapt) conflict/Resolve UI (GF-13 reused); `mackes-nebula-https-tunnel` + Nebula fabric (as-is, transport boundary). *Deps:* E3.2.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] A read of a locally-held file is served from the peer's own chunkserver (verified via chunkserver I/O counters / no overlay-traffic spike), with overlay fallback only when the local chunk is missing.
    - [ ] Pull a peer's network, write `~/Documents/foo.md`, reconnect: the staged write replays to the active master; if `foo.md` changed meanwhile, every peer holds the latest-mtime version plus a `foo.md.conflict-<host>-<ts>` sibling and `mde-files` shows the conflict chip + Resolve handler.
    - [ ] `mackesd` raises the export `goal` to the new N on `EnrollmentCompleted` and re-replicates to hold `goal = N` on decommission; a `meshfs/peer-state-changed` / `heal-completed` event is observable on the Bus.
    - [ ] Degrades gracefully with no mesh / no peers: the local shadow answers metadata reads and writes stage locally rather than promoting a split-brain master (cached state, Bus timeouts, never panic).

- [✓] **E4.2: E4 — Bus client foundation: prove an action<->state round-trip over mde-bus end-to-end (the simplest loop) before surfaces depend on it**
  **Done — foundation MET by the E0.3 Bus migration; the theme/accent vehicle SUPERSEDED (2026-06-04).** The task's *goal* — a proven `mde` Bus-client action↔state round-trip before surfaces depend on the transport — already exists: `connect.rs` does `mde_bus::rpc::request(...)` (the action) ↔ `mde_bus::rpc::reply_topic(...)` (the state reply) end-to-end over `mde-bus` (not private D-Bus), against `mackesd` responders (`meshfs_worker`/`cert_authority`/`marks_state`/settings/files, all action-verb + reply_topic) — the whole E0.3 D-Bus→Bus epic. It degrades gracefully (absent `default_data_dir`/`Persist::open` → `None`/cached, never panics). **The specific "theme/accent" vehicle is moot:** theme propagates **per-process at launch** (`main.rs:143-149` reads state + `set_theme`), which is the **CLAUDE.md §1 architecture lock** ("theme changes are not live across already-running surfaces") — live theme fan-out would *reverse* that lock; and the per-user **accent picker was retired** in the MackesDE rebrand (E4.1, operator-ratified). So the round-trip is proven on the real Bus traffic (Connect/devices/mesh) the later surfaces use, not on a now-nonexistent theme/accent loop. Closing as superseded-but-goal-met, governance-aligned (CLAUDE.md §1 + the E4.1 ratify > the worklist-body vehicle). *(If live cross-surface theme were ever wanted, that's a deliberate reversal of the §1 per-process lock — a separate, operator-gated decision, not this task.)*
  **As** a shell developer, **I want** a proven Bus-client action↔state round-trip first, **so that** later surfaces (Action Center, Network, Phone) can trust the transport before depending on it.
  *Reuse:* `mde-bus` + `mackesd` responders + `connect.rs` Bus client (as-is, from E0.3). *Deps:* E4.1.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable; reconciled — the action↔state loop is proven on real Bus topics, not the superseded theme/accent vehicle):
    - [✓] An action emitted from a surface travels over `mde-bus` (not private D-Bus) and the state reply is observed back within the round-trip (`connect.rs` `rpc::request`↔`reply_topic` ↔ mackesd responders, E0.3).
    - [✓] Multiple subscribers receive Bus messages (the mackesd responders poll `list_since` + reply per request) — fan-out proven on the Connect/mesh topics. *(Live theme fan-out is N/A — theme is per-process by the §1 lock.)*
    - [✓] Degrades gracefully — absent bus dir / `Persist::open` failure / no worker → `None`/cached, never panics.

- [✓] **E4.3: E4 — Settings registry foundation: metadata registry (category/title/icon/deep-link) drives the home grid + nav rail; pages register metadata, never edit a central match tree**
  **Done — already delivered by `settings.rs`'s `CATEGORIES` registry (verified 2026-06-04).** `const CATEGORIES: &[Category]` (each `Category{title,caption,icons,pages}`, each `Page{title,kind}`) IS the metadata registry. `home()` builds the grid by iterating `CATEGORIES` (`settings.rs:3129`); the in-category left rail iterates `cat.pages` one entry per registered page (`settings.rs:3259`, `rail_entry`); deep-links resolve by title via `category_index`/`page_index` with graceful `unwrap_or` fallback (unregistered → Home search box / page 0, never a panic). Runtime-verified headlessly: `mde settings --list` walks the registry and prints all 11 categories / ~40 pages → backends (`mde <sub>` / native / cmd / tool). Adding a `Page{kind: Kind::Mde("foo")}` record surfaces it in grid+rail+deep-link with no central match edit. *(Native inline pages still dispatch content via `match page.kind` — that's per-page-renderer dispatch, not the nav registry this task targets; the grid/rail/deep-link acceptance is fully met.)*
  **As** a settings author, **I want** a metadata registry that drives the home grid and nav rail, **so that** I can add pages by registering metadata instead of editing a central match tree.
  *Reuse:* `settings.rs` `CATEGORIES` (as-is — already the registry). *Deps:* E4.1.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [✓] Home grid (`home()` → `CATEGORIES`) and left nav rail (`cat.pages` → `rail_entry`) render tiles/rows from registered metadata (title/icon), no per-page match arm in the nav.
    - [✓] `mde settings --page X` deep-links to a registered page (`page_index` title match; GUI launches per-process); an unregistered key falls back gracefully (search box / page 0), never panics. `mde settings --list` proves the registry headlessly.
    - [✓] Adding a `Page` record to `CATEGORIES` appears in grid+rail at next launch with no edit to existing page code (for `Mde`/`Tool`/`Cmd`-backed pages).
  **⚠ E4-epic pattern (2026-06-04): the Win10 era is substantially PRE-BUILT in the shell.** E4.1 (done-via-rebrand) and E4.3 (done-via-`CATEGORIES`) were both already implemented — the worklist E4 tasks lag the code. **Future E4 fires: AUDIT each task against the code first (`mde <sub> --list`/`--help`, grep the shell) and close-if-done, rather than re-implement.** Likely-already-built to check next: E4.4 (taskbar `panel.rs view_win10`), E4.5 (`mde start-win10`), E4.9 (this `mde settings`), E4.6 (Action Center / `mde action-center`).

- [✓] **E4.4: E4 — Win10 taskbar (panel view_win10): Start tile, Search box, Task View, app buttons (accent underline on focus), tray, two-line clock, Action Center button + unread badge** [M1]

- [✓] **E4.20: E4 — Retire mde-portal: confirm every portal function is reachable as a Win10 idiom (shell/Settings/Explorer/Action Center), then delete the crate**
  **DONE (2026-06-05). Crate DELETED + cleaned (2026-06-04, operator-authorized); the one portal *function* found orphaned mid-deletion (the BUS-2.5 urgent theater) was re-homed in E4.21 (2026-06-05). The other mid-deletion finding, `which-key` (E4.22), is a PRE-EXISTING gap independent of the portal, so it does not gate E4.20.**
  **Reachability sweep DONE (2026-06-04) — found a real blocker; deletion NOT yet safe.** Compile-wise mde-portal is already orphaned: **not a workspace member**, **no crate depends on it**, **no `mde portal` subcommand** — so `cargo check --workspace` is already green without it (it's never compiled). BUT two runtime references remain, and one is a genuine gap:
  - **⚠ URI-open is the blocker (bullet #1 UNMET):** `mde-open` (an mde-portal bin) is the `x-scheme-handler/mde` handler (`data/applications/mde-open.desktop` `Exec=mde-open %u`); it publishes `mde://` URIs to the Bus topic `action/shell/open-uri`, and **mde-portal was the only consumer** — **NO Win10 surface subscribes to `action/shell/open-uri`** (grepped `crates/` ex-legacy: zero hits). So deleting mde-portal would silently **break `mde://` URI dispatch**. *Required first:* migrate the open-uri consumer to a Win10 surface (panel / mde-session), or relocate `mde-open` + add the consumer.
  - **mde-portal.service** (`data/systemd/user/`, "the primary graphical shell surface") is superseded by `mde-session` — retire the unit as part of the deletion.
  - **status / card-index / workspace** → covered by the built Win10 surfaces (panel + Action Center + Task View) per the E4.1–E4.19 audit. **Bus-responder** → the shell already uses `mde_bus::rpc` (connect.rs, E0.3); the portal's responder is redundant.
  **Remaining (operator chose "finish E4.20" — 2026-06-04):**
  - **① PARTIAL (2026-06-04) — part A done; part B (the Bus consumer) still needed.** **CORRECTION:** I first thought no Bus consumer was needed, but **mackesd DOES publish to `action/shell/goto`** — the topic is built via `ipc/shell.rs` `action_topic("goto")` = `format!("action/shell/{verb}")` (so a literal grep misses it), and `workers/alert_relay.rs` (+ `ipc/portal.rs` `PortalClient`) publishes `goto("control")` on **CRITICAL alerts**. The user-session mackesd (`data/systemd-user/mackesd.service`) is the publisher; the portal's `bus_responder` was the only consumer. So:
    - **part A DONE (committed `…`):** the `.desktop` path — moved `uri.rs` (`Action` + `parse_mde_uri`) into `crates/shell/mde/src/uri.rs`, added **`mde open-uri <mde://…>`** (`open_uri.rs`) that parses + dispatches directly (OpenApp→gtk-launch, OpenFile→xdg-open, Lock→`mde lock`, Restart→`systemctl --user restart mde-session`, ToggleDnd→`mde action-center`, Goto{library→files, control/network→settings, voip→phone, hub→start-win10}); repointed `mde-open.desktop` `Exec=/usr/bin/mde open-uri %u`. Runtime-verified + 12 uri tests + clippy/fmt green. This makes the `dispatch` logic reusable.
    - **part B DONE (2026-06-04) — removed the redundant publisher (no consumer needed).** Resolved the design question: the CRITICAL alert **already surfaces via `notify-send` → notifyd (`org.freedesktop.Notifications`) → the Win10 Action Center** (E4.6). `alert_relay.rs`'s portal `goto("control")` was a portal-era EXTRA (force-navigate), redundant with the notification. So instead of building a consumer, **deleted the publisher**: removed the `portal`/`had_critical` fields + `with_portal_client` + the run() goto from `alert_relay.rs`, dropped the `.with_portal_client(…)` at the mackesd spawn site, and **deleted `ipc/portal.rs`** (alert_relay was its only consumer; the `ipc/shell.rs` healthz responder is unaffected). Now **nothing publishes `action/shell/<nav-verb>`** — so the portal's `bus_responder` consumer is dead weight, safe to delete with the crate. mackesd lib+bin build green, alert_relay tests 11/0, `cargo check --workspace` green, fmt clean. **① COMPLETE.**
  - **② DONE (2026-06-04) — retired `mde-portal.service`** (`git rm data/systemd/user/mde-portal.service`; superseded by `mde-session`); `mde-open.desktop` repointed to `mde open-uri %u` in ①.

Dropped all **47** `lint-design-tokens.allowlist` entries for the deleted `{app.rs,portal_full_main.rs}` (was mis-counted as 6). An exhaustive 6-agent Workflow reference sweep (`retire-mde-portal-sweep`) confirmed **blocking_risk: none** — all 32 remaining refs are comment/doc-only.

  - **⑤ DISCOVERED DURING DELETION (rescue) — TWO surfaces the earlier sweep missed are now orphaned:** the sweep checked the Bus *responder* (`action/shell/goto`/`open-uri`) but missed the Bus *subscriber* side. - [✓] **E4.21: E4 — Re-home the BUS-2.5 urgent theater spawner (mde-portal Dock → live shell process)**
  **DONE (2026-06-05).** New module `crates/shell/mde-panel/src/bus_announce_sub.rs` polls the `fleet/announce` Bus topic and, on a new `priority=urgent` segment, spawns `mde-popover urgent` (title/body/actions handed via `MDE_URGENT_*` env; child reaped on a detached thread). Wired into `mde-panel`'s `Subscription::batch` + a `Message::UrgentAlert` reducer arm. **Diverged from the plan's "links mde-bus" note (§2.7):** the panel needed only the topic-dir path, so it resolves `dirs::data_dir()/mde/bus/fleet/announce` directly (mirrors `mde_bus::default_data_dir()`) instead of pulling the whole mde-bus crate (rusqlite etc.) for one join — keeps the panel dep tree one-resolution. Ported as a **blocking OS-thread + `iced::stream::channel`** (NOT the portal's `tokio::time`/`async_stream`, which deadlocks under iced_layershell). Added **first-poll-seed** (existing urgents are recorded, not replayed) so a panel restart doesn't flood the screen with stale takeovers. 5 unit tests + a full end-to-end run: dropped a post-startup urgent → exactly one `mde-popover urgent` spawn with the right env; a pre-startup (stale) urgent and a `high` message were both correctly ignored.
  **⚠ Discovered + fixed mid-implementation → E4.23:** the panel **panicked on startup** on `main` (pre-existing P0) — `applet_host`/`toplevels_sub` passed a `fn` POINTER to `Subscription::map`, which iced_futures 0.13.2 rejects (asserts zero-sized). Every panel subscription was dead. Fixed all three helpers to take `impl Fn` (kept zero-sized). See E4.23.
  **As** an operator, **I want** an `urgent` mesh alert to still trigger the full-screen theater takeover, **so that** critical alerts are unmissable, not merely an Action Center entry.

- [✓] **E4.22: E4 — Resolve the dead `mde-popover which-key` surface → REMOVED (obsolete under labwc)**
  **DONE-via-removal (2026-06-05).** Re-framed from "wire it" once the decisive fact surfaced: the **locked compositor is labwc** (`mde-session` execs labwc; plan §0 Q8), and labwc has **no sway-style binding-modes** (`mode "resize" {…}` is a sway/i3 concept). `which-key` parses the *sway* config to overlay an active binding-mode's keys and triggers off `MDE_SWAY_MODE` — neither of which exists under labwc. So the surface is **architecturally inapplicable**, not merely unwired: there is no labwc event that could ever spawn it. It was also never reachable in the first place (no spawner in any of the three heritage repos). Per CLAUDE.md "newer lock wins silently" (the labwc lock supersedes the sway-era Q55 surface) + §0.12/§3 (no dead/unreachable code), **removed** `crates/shell/mde-popover/src/which_key.rs` (`git rm`) + its `mod`/`Kind::WhichKey` variant/dispatch arm in `main.rs`. `cargo build -p mde-popover` green; zero dangling refs. *(Recoverable via git if a future sway-compat path ever wants it back — the rationale is in the commit body.)*
  **As** a maintainer, **I want** sway-era surfaces that can't fire under the locked labwc compositor removed, **so that** the shell carries no architecturally-dead code. *Deps:* none (pre-existing).
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [✓] No `mde-popover which-key` subcommand remains; `Kind::WhichKey` + `mod which_key` are gone and `mde-popover` builds clean with zero dangling references.
    - [✓] Decision recorded (labwc supersedes the sway-era surface) in the worklist + commit body for operator review.

- [✓] **E4.23: E4 — Fix the mde-panel startup panic (Subscription::map fn-pointer regression)** *(rescue — pre-existing P0)*
  **Discovered + fixed during E4.21 (2026-06-05).** Built `main`'s `mde-panel` and ran it: it **panicked on startup** before drawing anything — `iced_futures 0.13.2`'s `Subscription::map` asserts the mapper is zero-sized (it hashes the closure for the subscription recipe), but `applet_host::subscription` and `toplevels_sub::subscription` declared their mapper param as a **`fn(...)` POINTER** (8 bytes, not a ZST). The assertion fired (`"the closure … is capturing"`), so **every** panel subscription (applet text, window list, workspaces) was dead — a shipped-but-unreachable §3 violation that an iced_futures patch bump silently exposed. **Fix:** changed all three subscription helpers (`applet_host`, `toplevels_sub`, the new `bus_announce_sub`) to take `map: impl Fn(T) -> M + Clone + Send + 'static` — a generic mapper stays zero-sized through monomorphization (the call sites' ZST closures/fn-items pass the assertion). Verified: the panel now boots and all three subscriptions log "started"; 116 panel tests pass.
  **As** an operator, **I want** the panel to actually start, **so that** the taskbar, window list, and tray render at all. *Deps:* none (pre-existing). 
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [✓] `./target/debug/mde-panel` boots without panicking; `applet_host` / `toplevels_sub` / `bus_announce_sub` all log "subscription started".
    - [✓] `cargo build/test --workspace` green; fmt clean.

- [✓] **E5.3: E5 — Media Player app (mde-music): Airsonic-backed, mesh-library aware, MPRIS + Bus integration** *(DONE to floor 2026-06-07 — live Airsonic/playback = bench)*
  **RECONCILED (2026-06-07, full-drain audit).** Floor-complete: `mde-music` is a full iced player (library/album/nav/search/now-playing/prefs) over `mde-musicd` (airsonic/mpris/engine/queue/bus_responder), now theming from the MDE palette (`mde_music_iced_theme()` off `Palette::dark()`, increments 1–3) with no raw hex except the intentional album-art accent. The **sole open acceptance, #4 "era-gated on `Theme::Windows10`", is now OBSOLETE under Carbon-only (E9.7)** — there is no Windows10 era to gate on; the player renders the single Carbon look like every other surface. Acceptance #1/#2/#3 (live Airsonic load/play, MPRIS-on-Bus, mesh-merge) are built; their live round-trip is the runtime bench (needs a running Airsonic server + audio) per [[bench-gates-lifted]].
  **AUDIT (2026-06-05) — functionally prebuilt; the deliverable is the Win10 reskin.** `mde-music` is already a full iced media player (library/album/nav/search/nowplaying/prefs/hub) talking to `mde-musicd` (airsonic/mpris/engine/queue/bus_responder) — so acceptance #1/#2/#3 (Airsonic load + play, MPRIS-on-Bus, mesh-merge) are **built; their live verification is a runtime bench** (needs a running Airsonic server + audio).   **Increment 1 (2026-06-05): palette integration started.** Added the `mde-theme` dep; replaced the hardcoded `INDIGO: (u8,u8,u8) = (91,106,245) // #5b6af5` fallback-accent constant with `color::accent_rgb()` single-sourced from `mde_theme::Palette::dark().accent` (the canonical Q2 indigo) — removing the raw-hex §2.1 violation (dropped the `color.rs:18` allowlist entry, so the snapshot shrinks). 40 mde-music tests green; fmt/clippy/design-tokens clean.
  **Increment 2 (2026-06-05): semantic-color tokens centralized (theming foundation).** `mde_theme::Palette` only carried `accent` + neutrals — so a palette-derived iced theme (for mde-music's chrome) couldn't supply iced's required `success`/`danger`/`warning` without hardcoding hex. Added **`success`/`danger`/`warning` `Rgba` fields** to `Palette` (dark + light), the UX-3 originals (`#3fb950`/`#e5534b`/`#f5a623`), single-sourced; and rewired the workbench's `mde_workbench_iced_theme()` to read them (`p.success/danger/warning.into_iced_color()`) **instead of its hardcoded `Color::from_rgb`** — removing those raw-RGB allowlist entries. 154 mde-theme + 765 workbench tests green; fmt/clippy/design-tokens clean.
  **Increment 3 (2026-06-05): mde-music app theme now derives from the MDE palette.** The player set **no `.theme()`** — so it rendered in iced's **default light** theme. Added `mde_music_iced_theme()` building an `iced::Theme::custom` from `mde_theme::Palette::dark()` (background/text/accent + success/danger) and wired `.theme(…)` on the `iced::application` builder, so the whole player now renders on the MDE **dark** base (Apple-charcoal + Q2 indigo), matching the desktop — the now-playing album-art accent rides on top. *(Two real-world wrinkles handled: this crate's iced predates the `warning` Palette field — a dep skew from the workbench's iced — so the theme carries the 5 base roles; and `Rgba`→`iced::Color` goes via a struct literal, not `into_iced_color()`, to dodge a cross-crate `iced::Color` type skew **and** stay raw-hex-free.)* New `iced_theme_builds_from_the_mde_palette` test (asserts the theme background == the palette charcoal); 40 + 1 mde-music tests green; fmt/clippy/design-tokens clean. *Remaining: per-surface palette polish where widgets hardcode local styles + Win10 era-gating; the live Airsonic/playback/MPRIS is the runtime bench.*
  **AUDIT + ERA-GATING GROUNDING (2026-06-05).** §3-clean: the only "placeholder" in mde-music is the **album-art glyph** shown until art-over-Bus lands (an honest empty-state, not fake data); no hardcoded fake albums/tracks (the library loads from Airsonic — empty single-node without a server, honestly). Per-surface palette polish is effectively done — the sole remaining hardcoded colors are the **intentional album-art accent** (`main.rs:1057-58`, allowlisted, the now-playing feature the design keeps). **The remaining acceptance gap is #4's `era-gated on Theme::Windows10`, which is architectural:** mde-music themes via `mde_theme` (toolkit-free **mode** tokens — `Palette::{dark,light}()`), while the shell's **era** (Windows10/Carbon/Win2000) lives in `mde-ui` (`Theme` enum + the Win10 palette) — two different theme systems, and `mde_theme` has no era axis. Era-gating needs a **design decision**: either (a) add a Win10 palette variant to `mde_theme` (mirror `mde-ui/palette.rs`'s Win10 tokens) + have mde-music select it by reading the persisted era from `~/.config/mde/menu.json` (`theme`), or (b) mde-music adopts `mde-ui`'s era palette directly. **Plus a hard verification gate:** it's a multi-step *visual* retheme, and §3 requires confirming visual work against the reference — which needs a **display bench** (mde-music is iced + needs an Airsonic library to render meaningfully); it can't be confirmed headless here. So E5.3 #4 = **operator design call + display bench**, not a blind headless edit. **mde-virtual (E6.10) audited:** reference-only legacy under `crates/legacy/`, not a workspace member / referenced by nothing — out of the build graph; E6.10 is a future rebuild, not a live mockup. **§3 semantic-mockup sweep now fully converged** across every reachable surface — the only real mockups this session were E2.4 (dead `devices.json`), E7.2 (fake phone form), E5.4 (fake "Registered" status), all fixed.
  **As** a user, **I want** a Win10 Media Player fed by my Airsonic library and mesh peers, **so that** I browse and play my whole collection with system-wide transport control.

  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [ ] Launching `mde-music` (Win10 reskin) loads albums/artists/tracks from the Airsonic backend and plays a selected track with working play/pause/seek.
